  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2961442239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2961442239" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2961442239?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2961442239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11609551486230099559"><i>”Children ceased to be children when you put a sword in their hands. When you taught them to fight a war, then you armed them and put them on the front lines, they were not children anymore. They were soldiers.”</i><br/><br/>This book. I mean… <b>THIS BOOK</b>! *sighs deeply and shakes head*<br/>There is so much to be said about “The Poppy War” and I’m afraid I won’t even be able to put at least half of my thoughts into decent sentences. Because after finishing this book about a month ago <b>(A MONTH AGO!!!)</b> I still have tr</span>
  <span id="freeText11609551486230099559" style="display:none"><i>”Children ceased to be children when you put a sword in their hands. When you taught them to fight a war, then you armed them and put them on the front lines, they were not children anymore. They were soldiers.”</i><br /><br />This book. I mean… <b>THIS BOOK</b>! *sighs deeply and shakes head*<br />There is so much to be said about “The Poppy War” and I’m afraid I won’t even be able to put at least half of my thoughts into decent sentences. Because after finishing this book about a month ago <b>(A MONTH AGO!!!)</b> I still have troubles to sort out all of my feelings and thoughts. <br /><br /><b>“The Poppy War”</b> is a great book but it tackles a lot of serious topics and I guess that’s the reason why my heart always feels kind of heavy when I think about it. Of course there is a war raging in this book but there happen so many other things that it’s almost impossible not to flinch when you reach those final 40%. Think about every atrocity that’s ever happened and you get a good idea about what you’re going to read in this book. There’s genocide, rape, torture, self-harm… and that’s just me naming a few of the triggers that might come your way. <br /><br /><i>”War doesn’t determine who’s right. War determines who remains.”</i><br /><br />Let me tell you this: The longer you continue the worse it gets and even though this was masterfully done and I loved the world building and all the characters, there is still this strange undercurrent of heavy sadness and dread. Golyn Niis was so tough to read, I still get goose bumps when I think about it. This chapter was so, so, so, so damn hard to get through and I can’t remember the last time I read a book and felt that way. Maybe I never felt that way reading a book before. At least I can’t remember a single book that actually made me feel like this. I swear my stomach turned and I had troubles to breathe. I was feeling nauseous reading a book! Yes, it was that heavy! Everyone who already read the book will know what I’m talking about and to those who didn’t: It’s really as bad as everyone claims it to be! I got plenty of warnings but nothing prepared me for Golyn Niis!<br /><br /><i>”Amateurs obsess over strategy, Irjah had once told their class. Professionals obsess over logistics.”</i><br /><br />Still, despite this heavy feeling of uneasiness that always overcomes me when I think about “The Poppy War” this book was definitely worth reading! I loved the fantasy elements and the idea of powers from the gods! Plus I really enjoyed the chapters at Sinegard Academy and the chimei! What I loved the most was the representation of human nature though. I might be alone with this but it’s obvious that R.F. Kuang put a lot of effort into her characters and you could see it in the way they grow, develop and change. Their character arcs were so amazing to follow, I’m in awe! And before I continue to gush about them here, I might as well move to my character section instead. ;-P<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>This is my spoilery spoiler section and if you didn’t read the book already you better turn around and leave. If you’re still curious and don’t want to heed my warning you may proceed at your own risk! I mean I warned you, right? ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Rin:</b><br /><br /><i>”No – they couldn’t just do this to her. They might think they could sweep her away like rubbish, but she didn’t have to lie down and take it. She had come from nothing. She wasn’t going back to nothing.”</i><br /><br />Oh gods! Rin! I can’t believe what she did in the end and I can’t wrap my head around the fact that such a sweet and innocent girl could change that much! But it still happened and her descent was so heavy to watch. &gt;_&lt; I guess that’s what happens when you play with fire, quite literally in her case. She got addicted to the power and I’m so damn afraid of what she’s going to do next! I loved her defiance and strength at the beginning of the book, how she wanted to learn and did everything possible to achieve her goal. She was so determined and strong-willed! But then the war began and all those things happened and with every chapter Rin changed! She became something different, she hardened her heart, she lost her moral compass and made decisions that got her deeper and deeper into the rabbit hole! And then she did the unthinkable and I’m not sure if she’ll ever be able to return from that darkness again. T_T The ending broke my heart, for Rin, for the person she could have been for everything she <b>HAD</b> been before she came to Sinegard. She’s not the person she used to be and I find myself weeping for everything she lost and for what she became. =((( <br /><br /><i>”She didn’t want to be possessed. She wanted to remain free.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Then I will die on my feet,” she said. “I will die with flames in my hand and fury in my heart.”</i><br /><br /><i>”My god didn’t make me do anything,” she said. “The gods can’t make our choices for us. They can only offer their power, and we can wield it. And I did, and this is what I chose.” She swallowed. “I don’t regret it.”</i><br /><br /><i>”She was sane, she was convinced of it. She was whole. She had lost much, yes, but she still had her own mind. She made her decisions. She chose to accept the Phoenix. She chose to let it invade her mind.”</i><br /><br /><b>Altan:</b><br /><br /><i>”We’re the final front,” said Altan. “If we fail, this country’s lost.” He clapped her on the shoulder. “Excited?”</i><br /><br />Altan broke my heart. At first I had the same impression like everyone else: That he knows what he’s doing, that he’s in control and a perfect student/soldier but the more we got to see from him, the more it became obvious that he’s far from all those things! This boy was broken beyond repair and he hid it so well that no one ever noticed until it was too late! I can’t say that I liked his actions but I could understand why he acted the way he did! He was lashing out at everyone because he was like a wild animal that only saw threats and didn’t know how to react to kindness. Altan was unable to see that not everyone who confronted him wanted to do him harm. Which makes me sad on so many levels. =( That poor, poor boy! To be tortured like this, to get out of it alive, to live with his past and the knowledge that it might happen again. Just to live with everything he went through! To draw breath every day and to continue, to keep on moving! I can’t even begin to comprehend how he must have felt and I can’t put into words how strongly I feel for him. T_T And I don’t want to believe that he’s dead! He can’t be dead! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”I don’t know,” he said after a long moment. “I don’t know what I’m doing.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Altan’s fire drew as its source an unending hate. It was a deep, slow burn. She could almost taste it, the venomous intent, the ancient misery, and it horrified her.<br />How could one person hate so much?<br />What had happened to him?</i><br /><br /><b>Kitay:</b><br /><br /><i>”One urinating statue for my easily entertained friend.”<br />Rin blushed. “Kitay, I can’t.”<br />“It costs nothing.”<br />“It costs a lot to me,” she said.<br />Kitay placed the statue in her hand. “If you say one more thing about money, I’m leaving you to get lost.”</i><br /><br />I absolutely adored Kitay! He’s such a good friend and I loved that Rin and he became besties. =) Despite being fortunate enough to be one of the rich kids at Sinegard Academy he still reached out to her and became her friend. I think that’s what I loved about him the most, he didn’t care about titles or money, he just cared about the person and what it could do! Kitay is the living and breathing proof that good people exist and in the end his character was the only one that gave me any hope. Because despite all the things he witnessed and regardless of everything that happened to him, he still had moral values and acted according to them. In a world so harsh and cruel that it changed everyone around him, he still held on to his convictions and I loved him for it! &lt;333 <br /><br /><i>”There was a hard glint to his eyes that she had never seen in him before. He looked as if he had aged five years. He looked like his father. He was like a sword that had been sharpened, metal that had been tempered.”</i><br /><br /><b>Jiang:</b><br /><br /><i>”I am a mortal who has woken up, and there is power in awareness.”</i><br /><br />I really don’t know how to feel about Jiang! I actually liked him at the beginning of the book but I was so disappointed by him when it ended. His character was some sort of catalyst and I had the distinct feeling that he could have done more, that he SHOUD HAVE done more! What if he would have taught Rin about her powers? What if he would have allowed her to use them in a safe setting? What if he would have fought alongside them and would have helped her to control the phoenix? He basically left Altan and Rin to their own devices and this set them on the dark path they were descending at the end. How different everything could have gone if Jiang would have watched out for them! =( To drop Altan as his student was the first mistake he made and not to teach Rin properly apparently his last. <br /><br /><i>”Ah. The law.” Jiang sniffed at an unidentified leaf and then tossed it away. “So inconvenient. So irrelevant.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Rin &amp; Altan:</u><br /><br /><i>”She knew what addiction looked like. Opium smokers were yellowed, useless sacks of flesh. They did not fight like Altan did. They did not move like Altan did. They were not perfect, lethal animals of graceful beauty.”</i><br /><br />Okay, I’m going to say it: <b>I DIDN’T SHIP RIN AND ALTAN!</b> I’m sorry but I just couldn’t! They didn’t have much of a relationship before Rin joined the Cike and once she was a part of them her relationship with Altan was nothing but abusive. He slapped her, hurt her with words, forced her to do things she didn’t want to do and was everything else but supportive. How was I supposed to ship that? I get that Altan was thoroughly broken but he didn’t have to let it out on Rin and as frustrated as he might have been with her, he still had no right to hurt her. So nope, it was clear right from the beginning that he didn’t respect her as much as she respected him and if you ask me those two never had a future. (Not saying that I wouldn’t love for Altan to come back again. I still wouldn’t ship him with Rin though) I’ll never ship those two and I stand by it. Fight me! *lol* ;-P<br /><br /><i>”Hey. Hey.”<br />Cool fingers wrapped around her wrists. Gently, Altan pulled her hands away from her face. She looked up and met his eyes. They were a shade of crimson brighter than poppy petals.<br />“It’s okay,” he said. “I know. I know what it’s like. I’m going to help you.”</i><br /><br /><i>”She had adored an idea of him, an archetype, a version of him that was invulnerable. But now she knew the truth, she knew the realness of Altan and his vulnerabilities and most of all his pain… and still she loved him.”</i><br /><br /><i>He leaned forward and grasped her face in both hands. She thought for a bizarre moment that he was going to kiss her. He didn’t. He pressed his forehead against hers for a long time. She closed her eyes. She drank in the sensation of her skin against his. She seared it into her memory.”</i><br /><br /><u>Rin &amp; Nezha:</u><br /><br /><i>”We aren’t here to be sophisticated. We’re here to fuck people up.”</i><br /><br />Now that’s a relationship I could appreciate! Yes, Nezha was an ass at the beginning of the book but in contrast to Altan he actually realized his faults and apologized to Rin. I loved how they both grew out of their initial animosity and became friends in the end. And those fighting scenes!! They were pure harmony on the battlefield and anyone who claims differently didn’t read the book! XD Just like Kitay seemed to have become a moral compass for Rin the same could be said for Nezha and I’m sure if he’d been around at the end she wouldn’t have gone down that dark road. &gt;_&lt; Unfortunately Nezha was lost in the toxic mist and seems to be dead. I refuse to believe that he’s gone for good though. I mean he had some serious healing abilities so maybe he survived it and became a prisoner? But then again he most likely would have been with the Mugenese when Rin launched her attack and I don’t know if he would have been able to survive this as well. &gt;_&lt; I really hope Nezha will magically reappear in the second book! =)<br /><br /><i>”But I saved your life. Doesn’t that make us at least a little square?”<br />Square? Square? She had to laugh. “You almost got me expelled!”<br />“And you almost killed me,” he said. That shut her up.<br />“I was scared of you,” Nezha continued. “And I lashed out. I was stupid. I was a spoiled brat. I was a real pain in the ass. I thought I was better than you, and I’m not. I’m sorry.”</i><br /><br /><u>Altan &amp; Chaghan:</u><br /><br /><i>”They had come to an understanding, she and Chaghan. They were no longer opposed, vying for Altan’s favor. They were allies, now, bound by the mutual atrocities they had commited.”</i><br /><br />I’m going to be honest here: I’m such a sucker for Chaghan!!! I love his character!!!! And is it just me or did I actually feel some gay vibes between those two?! Altan and Chaghan definitely had more chemistry than Rin and Altan ever had! *lol* And they didn’t even have all too many scenes together! I got the distinct feeling that something happened when they spent those three days in the valleys and I’m not talking about Altan winning a fight between them, feel me? *wriggles eyebrows* Haha! ;-P Gosh, I really would have loved to find out more about their relationship and this is just one more reason why Altan can’t be dead! I just ship him and Chaghan too much to accept his death! Period! XD<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br /><b>“The Poppy War”</b> was an amazing and sometimes truly revolting dark tale about a young girl that follows her own path and fights for what she thinks is right. It shows us how people can grow and how their circumstances and perceptions can change them. For better or for worse… This tale isn’t over yet. In fact it just began and I can’t wait to read what’s going to happen next. Let’s continue to hope for the best while we expect the worst, because apparently that’s the only attitude that will get you through this series. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”And she would call the gods to do such terrible things.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11609551486230099559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2356358017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14437494975503556143"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525028370i/25453966._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But I warn you, little warrior. The price of power is pain.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>First and foremost, please go read one of my best friends in this entire world’s review: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2276617449' rel='nofollow noopener'>Petrik’s review</a> is not only amazing, he is also an ownvoices Chinese reviewer. Next, I just want to warn you guys that this is a very dark book that is heavily inspired by the <a href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanking_Massacre' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nanking Massacre</a>. Please use caution and know that this book has major <b>trigger and co</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14437494975503556143" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525028370i/25453966._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But I warn you, little warrior. The price of power is pain.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>First and foremost, please go read one of my best friends in this entire world’s review: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2276617449" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik’s review</a> is not only amazing, he is also an ownvoices Chinese reviewer. Next, I just want to warn you guys that this is a very dark book that is heavily inspired by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanking_Massacre" rel="nofollow noopener">Nanking Massacre</a>. Please use caution and know that this book has major <b>trigger and content warnings</b> for war themes, drug use, substance addiction, self-harm, racism, misogyny, genocide, bullying, abandonment, abuse, animal death, animal cruelty, brutal torture, brutal killing, brutal rape (off screen, but still maybe the worst I’ve ever read), mutilation, very graphic depictions of how children and adults died, experimentations on people against their will, colorism, colonization. Again, this is a very dark book that carries some very dark themes. Please use caution.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“War doesn’t determine who’s right. War determines who remains”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>The Poppy War</i> is a fantastic debut that I feel so very privileged to have received an ARC of. This is the first book in an ownvoices Asian inspired fantasy story, and this first installment is told in three parts; each getting darker and darker. But in part one we meet our main protagonist, Rin, who is a war orphan who is living with a foster family that was forced to adopt her. <br><br>Rin has been working at the family’s local business, while also being forced to deal drugs. That is, until one day her family decided that it would be more in their interest for them marry Rin off to a man who is much older than her and who she has never met before. Rin is then forced to do the only thing that will allow her to not have this life forced upon her. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Well, fuck the heavenly order of things. If getting married to a gross old man was her preordained role on this earth, then Rin was determined to rewrite it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In this world, children will study their entire lives for a test called the Keju. And the top fifty students in the country will be allowed to go the empire’s capitol to study at the best military school in the world. There they will be able to become the world’s best generals, tacticians, soldiers, and more. And all the students wish to one day be warriors for the Empire. And Rin dedicates herself to studying so that she can not only escape this marriage, but to also escape her abusive foster parents, and the entire town that has treated her awful just because she was born a war orphan. <br><br>And against all odds, Rin gets accepted. But once she gets to the school, she soon realizes that her spot isn’t guaranteed to last. At the end of the year, the different teachers will pick which students they wish to have study under them. And Rin soon starts to see that most of the school is not only very privileged, but also have power just from their last name and who their family is already in the current military. <br><br>And the reason part one of this book is hands down my favorite is because I love this school setting so much. And like many other reviewers have already said, it is very reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301719771" rel="nofollow noopener">The Name of the Wind</a>. From the attending kids that have been born with a silver spoon in their mouths, to unexpected companionship, to horrible teachers, to wonderfully odd teachers. And Rin becomes obsessed with not only impressing these teachers and her peers, but to prove that she is also deserving of her spot. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You’re a war orphan. You’re a southerner. You weren’t supposed to pass the Keju. The Warlords like to claim that the Keju makes Nikan a meritocracy, but the system is designed to keep the poor and illiterate in their place. You’re offending them with your very presence.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And while Rin is working to become the best at her school, terrible things are brewing outside the walls of the academy. Terrible, unthinkable things, that are about to impact the whole world. And Rin is forced to quickly learn about another world all together, where gods can make a person a shaman that can wield that power, but at a cost. And Rin has to discover for herself if the price is worth it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The nature of this god is to destroy. The nature of this god is to be greedy, to never be satisfied with what he has consumed.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is an action packed read, with beautiful writing that feels like a treat to read. This is a story filled with twists and turns, and you might think you know where the story is going, to only be completely dumbfounded. I couldn’t flip the pages fast enough. <br><br>Also, there is sort of an enemies to friends (maybe lovers eventually) element in this book, and I’m dying to see more in book two. Like, there is going to be more of it? Right? Please. Seriously, what God do I have to let inhabit my body? I need it. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Because I can,” she said. “Because he thought he could get rid of me. Because I want to break his stupid face.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And ultimately, this is a story about a girl who has been given nothing but pain in a world that constantly reminds her that she is lesser. And she overcomes every single hurdle and becomes not only what the world said she couldn’t be, but she becomes what she wanted to be. Like, this book is powerful, empowering, and a love letter to all girls that are told they can’t do something daily. <br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed this one, even if it got even a little too dark for me at times. I think this is a really amazing set up for what is sure to be an impressive debut fantasy series! I cannot wait to see what R.F. Kuang does next, because I really think <i>The Poppy War</i> is a bright shining star in 2018 releases. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="14437494975503556143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2463118763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10823075688792546239"><b>Low 3 Stars</b><br/><br/>Boy, did it take me forever to finish this thing.<br/><br/><b>I <i>really</i> wanted to love this book.</b> One of my favorite reviewers adored it and sang it's praises, but it just didn't draw me in the way I thought it would. <br/><br/>The last 150 pages or so got really good (thus why I rated it 3 instead of the possible 2 I was planning on up until that point - not that it matters) and I smashed through them in one sitting; however, it still didn't save the entire book for me. <br/><br/>I felt that the world-building was lo</span>
  <span id="freeText10823075688792546239" style="display:none"><b>Low 3 Stars</b><br /><br />Boy, did it take me forever to finish this thing.<br /><br /><b>I <i>really</i> wanted to love this book.</b> One of my favorite reviewers adored it and sang it's praises, but it just didn't draw me in the way I thought it would. <br /><br />The last 150 pages or so got really good (thus why I rated it 3 instead of the possible 2 I was planning on up until that point - not that it matters) and I smashed through them in one sitting; however, it still didn't save the entire book for me. <br /><br />I felt that the world-building was loose and the magic system somewhat unclear. I also felt like I never truly got to know the characters. Their characterizations were very surface-level...and completely inconsistent to boot. I didn't like our protagonist, Rin (I thought she acted like a whiny child who threw tantrums every now and then) and, other than Altan, almost all the other characters felt like one big blob of background noise with no truly defining characteristics or story lines of their own. <br /><br />Thus, I spent the entirety of the book not really knowing for what or whom I should (or wanted) to root. And I'm a rooter. I need to know whose side I'm on, especially in my fantasy. <br /><br />I <i>might</i> continue with book 2 when/if it comes out as it's possible I will love that whole book to the level I loved the last 150 pages of this one; but we shall see. <br /><br />Regardless, I know I am very much in the minority with this book, so I would encourage you to still give it a go if it was something that caught your eye.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2883564045" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2883564045" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2883564045?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-poc-asian">rep-poc-asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=my-soul-hurts">my-soul-hurts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=shocking">shocking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=please-step-on-me">please-step-on-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=rep-poc-asian-author">rep-poc-asian-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=ownvoices">ownvoices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-3rd">pov-3rd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-female">pov-female</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2883564045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14315033317669110094"><b>what I should be thinking:</b> The Poppy War explores themes of power, ambition, and humanity with a skill that is thoroughly inspiring for an author only 21 years old at the time of publishing, and Kuang expertly develops Rin into a character you hate yet also, somehow, adore. The book snakes its way through your brain, subtly becoming an obsession that only grows as time passes, and each day you find yourself thinking about how <i>perfect</i> of a book it is.<br/><br/><b>what I’m actually thinking:</b> Fang Runin please </span>
  <span id="freeText14315033317669110094" style="display:none"><b>what I should be thinking:</b> The Poppy War explores themes of power, ambition, and humanity with a skill that is thoroughly inspiring for an author only 21 years old at the time of publishing, and Kuang expertly develops Rin into a character you hate yet also, somehow, adore. The book snakes its way through your brain, subtly becoming an obsession that only grows as time passes, and each day you find yourself thinking about how <i>perfect</i> of a book it is.<br /><br /><b>what I’m actually thinking:</b> Fang Runin please step on me.<br /><br />—★—<br /><br />It feels like my life has been split into two eras: Before The Poppy War, and After The Poppy War.<br /><br />There is no way to write a review that encompasses both my love for and the literary excellence of this book, and there are already some brilliant reviews out there (my personal favorites are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2276617449?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik’s</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2389208847?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Jami’s</a>). But my feelings about this book have grown to become an irritating cramp in my side, constantly pestering me: I genuinely cannot stop thinking about it every day. There is a burgeoning need in me to get something written down before I spontaneously combust.<br /><br />The Poppy War follows a girl named Rin, a dark-skinned poor orphan who, to everyone’s surprise, manages to get into Nikan’s prestigious military academy Sinegard. There, she is relentlessly bullied for her skin color, gender, and economic status, yet she works tirelessly and climbs to the top of her class. But war is looming, and soon, with the dangerous, destructive shamanic powers she accidentally accessed, she shifts from student to soldier and <b>is forced to make difficult decisions to save her country</b>.<br /><br />I think my favorite thing about the entire book—which is a grand statement to make considering how excellent it is in every aspect—is Rin. Her character development is phenomenal, and not only in terms of who she becomes in the story, but also just Kuang’s ability to craft a character so well. It’s made clear from the very start that whether or not you like Rin is up for you to decide, and this idea only grows as Rin begins to make questionable choices.<br /><br />But god, if you don’t find yourself rooting for her, at least in the beginning, I’m not sure you get the point at all: Rin is a girl who, throughout her entire life, has fought against every person who tells her she is a burden and she is lesser, every obstacle that represents how her very own existence is an inferiority. And she never stops fighting. <b>Everything Rin does is a pushback against her oppressors</b>: gaining power, becoming a top student, turning into the perfect warrior and soldier (or… mostly perfect), and most of all using her anger and desire for vengeance as a motivation. Many of her actions are morally ambiguous, but you always understand the reasoning behind them, and whether or not you like her or agree with what she does, you still can’t help but feel a keen sense of both compassion and sadness for her.<br /><br />(I love her so much. I love her so, so much.)<br /><br />Kuang also writes other characters just as complex as Rin, most notably Altan. He is the sole survivor of a massacre that destroyed his race, and his life has only consisted of suffering and trauma. Now he’s seen only as a weapon to use to the Nikara military’s advantage. And it’s heartbreaking to see his rage fester, because it’s the one thing he’s ever known, and this hatred and desire for vengeance against Nikan was brought upon themselves for the things they did to his race. <br /><br />Rin and Altan share many characteristics—Altan is her commander and role model—a large one being that neither of them are seen as human. I will never stop losing my mind and being desperately sad over how they are seen as risky yet powerful weapons but disposable once used, and how this <b>view of them is exactly what shaped them into who they are now</b>, is exactly why they do the things they do. Their complex relationship is written so masterfully, especially in the sequel The Dragon Republic, and I feel like I could wail about them forever. I may not love Altan, but I still appreciate the way that Kuang makes me mind-blown over his development.<br /><br />I also don’t want to forget Kitay and Nezha, who are some of Rin’s classmates that I love a lot. They’re both assholes, in all honesty, but it’s part of their charm! I feel like they are more developed in The Dragon Republic, as this installment seems to focus more on Altan, but they still have important roles in Rin’s life, as the only friend she had in Sinegard and her bully-turned-friend(-turned-LOVER?), respectively.<br /><br />(I guess my one complaint for the entire book is that there are some side characters, specifically the members of the Cike, who are not that developed. But that’s my only critique and it’s so minor that it is practically irrelevant! I also didn’t care that much because, if it isn’t obvious, I pretty much just care about Rin.)<br /><br />On top of the excellent character work, Kuang succeeds in many other areas of the book as well. The way war is depicted stands out the most: She does not shy back, and I didn’t want her to. It’s brutal and graphic and most definitely difficult to read (content warnings at the end), but the way it viscerally tears at you is unforgettable and that’s the exact kind of effect it should have. <b>It’s a harsh reminder of how viciously cruel humans can be</b>, especially when you realize that what happens in the book is based on real-life historical events. You question over and over again, <i>What lets humans do this to one another? How can such wicked violence be justified? How can people commit atrocities and not feel an ounce of remorse?</i> and if that isn’t the lovely, jarring reading experience I want!!<br /><br />A good fantasy must have good worldbuilding, and The Poppy War doesn’t disappoint in this aspect either. I’m not usually one to notice worldbuilding unless it stands out, either in a really good or really bad way, and <b>Kuang’s worldbuilding is definitely on the really good side of the spectrum</b>. Shamanism, gods, and magic are among the fantastical elements of the worldbuilding. The concept you usually see in fantasy of “magic is glorious and practicing it makes you healthier” is subverted into “magic can destroy you and you risk insanity each time you call upon the gods” and I <i>adored</i> it, especially when looking at it through the lens of how it furthered Rin’s character development. (Again, if it’s not clear yet, I! love!! Rin!!!)<br /><br />Just the geographic worldbuilding was enjoyable to me as well—the explorations of colonialism and imperialism are so well-done. The way it mirrors our world, with China, Japan, and the West, is also something I really adore, because it depicts the horrific war crimes that Japan has committed while also painting the West as, dare I say it, the larger evil. (This is developed more in book 2 than in book 1, but I think it’s still worth mentioning.)<br /><br />The final cherry on top, though, is Kuang’s prose and ability to write everything in a deeply compelling way. <b>It’s simple and lovely and engaging</b>, and it fits perfectly with the heavy content. This book is one that I chose to read for an English project, and for one of my assignments I talked about how there aren’t too many details in her writing, yet somehow I can imagine everything clearly and her words still have a strong emotional impact. (This assignment was a video that ended up being over 20 minutes long because, clearly, I cannot shut up about this book.)<br /><br />It’s also worth noting that I struggle a lot to get through long adult fantasy novels, but this one was an exception. If you’re looking for an easier to read adult fantasy in terms of dense or heavy writing, I definitely recommend this one. I kept reading 100 pages in one sitting before realizing I had to stop reading, and everything seemed to fly by so quickly. It’s a wonder how 500+ pages can feel like nothing, yet I think back on this book and feel a strange flurry of excitement at the prospect of rereading it all within a day.<br /><br />I’ve been writing this review for around three hours now (even though it feels like no time has passed because I could go on and on about this book). It’s certainly not my best, and there is so much more I could say to display how this book is absolute perfection. I don’t know if there’s someone out there who still hasn’t read this yet, but if there is, imagine me on my knees begging you to read it and <b>experience the masterpiece that is The Poppy War for yourself</b>. Rin will forever remain one of my favorite characters <i>(step on me step on me step on me)</i>, and I won’t be getting over this book for a long time. It’s genuinely one of the best I’ve ever read, both subjectively and objectively, and I cannot recommend it enough!<br /><br />—★—<br /><br /><i><b>:: rep ::</b> Asian-inspired (mainly Chinese-) cast<br /><br /><b>:: content warnings ::</b> war themes (death, murder, violence, etc.), drug use, substance addiction, self-harm, racism, colorism, misogyny, genocide, bullying, abandonment, abuse, animal death, animal cruelty, brutal &amp; graphic torture, killing &amp; rape, mutilation, human experimentation</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14315033317669110094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2411873399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2411873399" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2411873399?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Grimdark junkies </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2411873399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10952011788424607071"><i>The Poppy War</i> is not a book to be missed by fantasy fans and especially those who like it infused with <b>copious amounts of blood, darkness and misery.</b> <br/><br/>This isn’t some fluffy little tale about teenage romance and personal discovery (although it may seem that way in the beginning.) This is a book about reality. Now that’s an odd thing to say isn’t it? Reality? We’re talking about fantasy here. But do let me explain. <br/><br/>This is a book about the realities of war. War isn’t pretty. War isn’t about heroic</span>
  <span id="freeText10952011788424607071" style="display:none"><i>The Poppy War</i> is not a book to be missed by fantasy fans and especially those who like it infused with <b>copious amounts of blood, darkness and misery.</b> <br /><br />This isn’t some fluffy little tale about teenage romance and personal discovery (although it may seem that way in the beginning.) This is a book about reality. Now that’s an odd thing to say isn’t it? Reality? We’re talking about fantasy here. But do let me explain. <br /><br />This is a book about the realities of war. War isn’t pretty. War isn’t about heroics and grand deeds. War is about men pissing themselves and running away in fear. War is about control. War is about men trying to murder each other; it’s about soldiers brutalising their enemies and terrorising the innocent. War is about rape, raping of the land and of the defenceless. None of us will ever be ready for it. It is so very unsurprising that Rin turns into a cold hearted bitch by the end. <br /><br /><i>“Children ceased to be children when you put a sword in their hands. When you taught them to fight a war, then you armed them and put them on the front lines, they were not children anymore. They were soldiers.” </i><br /><br /> Her student days are over before they really began. She only just begins to taste her power (a rage filled magic fuelled by drugs) before she is enlisted and forced to defend her training academy from invaders. Her master taught her to control her power, and trained her only to understand it. He never wanted her to use it, though when backed into a corner Rin unleashes all her fiery fury upon her enemies. It was either that or death. Some will think her character extreme, though I think she is a product of her situation. <br /><br />Rin is driven to succeed. This is not a woman who will give up. She has done some excessive things to be admitted into the training academy. She has gone without sleep. She has self-harmed (to allow the former) and she has worked harder than most would think possible. The war has shattered her dreams. It has prevented her from finishing her studies and it has turned her into a killer. She wants to finish it and will do absolutely anything possible to do so, vengeance becomes her new goal. By the end she is unrecognisable even to herself. War has killed her in a way, though it has made her very strong. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <u>“War doesn't determine who's right. War determines who remains.”</u>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><i>The Poppy War</i> was not the book I thought it would be. The more fantasy I read, the more I see the same similar plot directions and romances. Some details were predictable (such as The Gatekeeper’s identity) though I did not expect it to go quite the way it did. Initially the book parallels much of the basic plot of <i>The Name of the Wind.</i> It appeared to be going in a similar direction but then the invaders came and everything exploded into a bloody mess of unpredictability. Such is the nature of war.<br /><br />This was far from a bad thing. I did really like the first part of the story, though my interest peaked as chaos descended. War never comes at the right time. It interrupts lives (and plots.) What the author showed us here is that it destroys everything. It destroys our plans and it destroys the direction we set for ourselves, and that’s why the sharp shift in plot was so necessarily strong. <br /><br /><b>Believe the hype. Believe the reviewers. This will be the biggest fantasy debut this year: go read it! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10952011788424607071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2614037658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2614037658" />
    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2614037658?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008239848" href="/book/show/40022965-the-poppy-war">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">grim military fantasy fans (not grimdark)</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mary by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4325322-tabi">TABI⁷ (ᕗツ)ᕗ</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=sociology">sociology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=religion">religion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2614037658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9513389979489155662"><b>When you are so hyped for a book you’re practically giving helium a run for its money, there are only 3 possibilities:</b><br/><br/><blockquote>☆ You write a pungent review, crushed beneath the waves of disappointment.<br/>✯ You write a loving criticism, pleased that it was good but displeased that it was not <i>that</i> good.<br/>★ You write a gushing piece, declaring your heart stolen and your soul sold.</blockquote><br/>I was hoping for the third.<br/>But I’ll settle for the second.<br/><br/><blockquote>
<img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601991625ra/30200670.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Credit: <a href='http://instagram.com/jhocaaa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jhoca</a>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <br/>
  <i>“You will be offered power beyond your imagination. But</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9513389979489155662" style="display:none"><b>When you are so hyped for a book you’re practically giving helium a run for its money, there are only 3 possibilities:</b><br><br><blockquote>☆ You write a pungent review, crushed beneath the waves of disappointment.<br>✯ You write a loving criticism, pleased that it was good but displeased that it was not <i>that</i> good.<br>★ You write a gushing piece, declaring your heart stolen and your soul sold.</blockquote><br>I was hoping for the third.<br>But I’ll settle for the second.<br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601991625ra/30200670.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Credit: <a href="http://instagram.com/jhocaaa" rel="nofollow noopener">Jhoca</a>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <br>
  <i>“You will be offered power beyond your imagination. But I warn you, little warrior. The price of power is pain.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Even as <i>The Poppy War</i> was not the perfection I’d dreamt it would be, I could not help but be awed by the exquisite detail of this rigorous craft where no misstep is excused and no strategy overlooked. From economy to dialects and sources of prejudice, Kuang has considered everything in spinning this yarn of war orphans and martial artists, with <b>gods that were only relics of the past peeking their insatiable heads and demanding blood as worship, and life beared in all its sheer dreadful abomination where an accident of birth makes all the difference because power, dolorously, dictates acceptability.</b><br><br>Through the duality of hallucinogens and the precarious line they make one dangle on, to studying opaque syllogisms and the intricate science of fighting at a ruthless military academy where girls cannot succeed unless they give up any future of motherhood, embarking on philosophical debates I craved to insert myself into on reality, brutality, and divinity, this debut mixes history and myth with fiction to paint an ancient China anew.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The fish does not attempt to fly. The polecat does not attempt to swim. Only when each being respects the heavenly order may there be peace.”<br>Well, fuck the heavenly order of things.</i>
</blockquote><br>But you cannot write military fantasy in all its glorious deception and spark a grim war’s inception without delving into tactics and logistics, and TPW is more analogous to a game of Go, treading strategy rather than direct confrontation to achieve dominance—despite the present action. <b>This is an empire that can never be ready to face the enemies within and without; this is a song of vengeance horrendous and wondrous in its entirety. What Kuang does, in the end, is to depict the invidious truth that war is not about rightness but survival; and as she would tell you, to explain gravity to a child you will first have to let them fall.</b><br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601991625ra/30200669.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Credit: <a href="http://instagram.com/jhocaaa" rel="nofollow noopener">Jhoca</a>
</blockquote><br>Sadly though, I did not close the book with everyone’s shared <i>what did I just read</i> sentiment but with a sigh of <i>ugh finally</i>, since the plot of the book was not all that unexpected due to most of the twists having been revealed to us before they were to the characters, and their eventual deliverance was not dramatic enough to warrant true shock. I admittedly preferred the engrossing trials of Part I to the passivity of what followed.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988119i/30200514._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
<b><u>CW</u></b> ➾ racism, colourism, colonisation, abuse, bullying, misogyny, use of psychedelics, drug addiction, self-harm, animal cruelty, nonconsensual human experimentations, torture, rape, burning, massacre, genocide, mutilation</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988119i/30200514._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Which Is It: <i>Grimdark or Wuxia Fantasy?</i></u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It’s rather bewildering to see various readers shelving the same book under 2 genres as fundamentally different as grimdark and wuxia fantasy. Like, what the hell? I’ll tell you what the hell.<br><br>✿ <b>
  <i>What is grimdark and is this it?</i>
</b> Adam Roberts puts grimdark as “<i>where nobody is honourable and Might is Right</i>,” declaring the world a “<i>cynical, disillusioned, ultraviolent place.</i>” Or as Genevieve Valentine puts it, grimdark dives into “<i>the psychology of those sword-toting heroes, and the dark realism behind all those kingdom politics</i>.” Even more complete is Jared Shurin’s 3 key components: a grim and dark tone, a sense of realism, and the agency of the protagonists versus predestination. Yes, this <i>can</i> all apply to TWP, especially if you consider the final theme that <b>heroes inevitably let you down and gods have no agency and it is <i>you</i> who will forge the path.</b> But in truth, TWP is not amoral or violent for the majority of the book. Why?<br><br>Because even as characters hold on to their anger throughout, they are so very concerned with morals and it’s only at the very end where they truly find law inconvenient in the face of their revenge. Because while there is violence aplenty in these pages, and while the logic of violence is explored and deaths are avenged, <b>that violence is noted as <i>wrong</i> and intentional brutality warned against on principle—it’s not until the very end where the protagonist looks at that violence and sees it as <i>right</i>.</b><br><br>My favourite definition of grimdark is Liz Bourke’s, “<i>a retreat into the valorisation of darkness for darkness’s sake, into a kind of nihilism that portrays right action as either impossible or futile.</i>” But this definition can only describe the end of TWP, which is just not enough. <b>I would say, pick this up for something grim and dark, but not for grimdark.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I am a mortal who has woken up, and there is power in awareness.”</i>
</blockquote><br>✿ <b>
  <i>What is wuxia and is this it?</i>
</b> Wuxia is a primarily historical genre of Chinese fantasy about a martial artist who follows the code of xia (<i>its 8 common attributes being: benevolence, justice, individualism, loyalty, courage, truthfulness, disregard for wealth, and desire for glory</i>). This theme of chivalrous righteousness might seem the opposite of all this book stands for, but wuxia heroes also remove oppressors and bring retribution for past misdeeds, and those 8 criteria <i>are</i> the focus of the first part of TPW—<b>before they’re twisted and turned on their heads for a darker approach, that is.</b><br><br>One type of wuxia fiction more common in the era of anti-Qing revolutionaries (<i>which is the era that inspired this series</i>) goes like this: A hero from the lower social class of ancient China is denied admission into a martial arts sect, so she experiences hardships and trains secretly, waiting to surprise those who looked down on her; the plot will meander to a final showdown between the protagonist and her nemesis. As you can see, this is the structure of TPW Part I and its themes are taken along throughout the military path of the book even as they are ingeniously reversed.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You’ll die.”<br>“Then I will die on my feet,” she said. “I will die with flames in my hand and fury in my heart. I will die fighting for the legacy of my people.”</i>
</blockquote><br>✿ <b>
  <i>Conclusion?</i>
</b> If I were to shelve this genre-bending debut, the first 50% would be wuxia, the next 40% military, and the last 10% grimdark fantasy. Ultimately, this book might be grimly stark, but it’s not grimdark. Perhaps more a wuxia gone dark.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988119i/30200514._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Asian Influences: <i>Historical &amp; Mythological</i></u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Starting from basics, compare this map with East Asia but keep in mind that the author said all resemblances to real-world countries are “<i>completely unintentional</i>” so shhhh:<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601992682i/30200709._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>Unfortunately, I can’t hush.<br><br>❀ <b>
  <i>Nikan is China</i>
</b> ➾ Evident in the usage of Chinese zodiac cycles for marking the passage of time and signs for naming the provinces; cì kè (<i>lit. assassin</i>) for the Cike; qi or ch'i (<i>life force or energy flow, the central principle in Chinese martial arts</i>) for ki; the expansionist policies and civilising mission alluding to the Qing dynasty (<i>the last imperial dynasty of China, 1636-1912</i>); Ke Ju (<i>the national examination system that became ossified during the Qing dynasty</i>) for Keju; The Art of War by Sun Tzu (<i>pinyin: Sūnzǐ</i>) for Sunzi’s Principles of War.<br><br>❀ <b>
  <i>Federation of Mugen is Japan</i>
</b> ➾ Due to themes of militarism and beliefs in the meaninglessness of the lives of soldiers and inhumanity of the non-Japanese, as well as the divinity of the Emperor practiced in Japan before the reconstruction.<br><br>❀ <b>
  <i>Speer is Taiwan</i>
</b> ➾ Mostly geographically but also Taiwan’s fight against colonisation by China.<br><br>❀ <b>
  <i>The Hinterlands are Mongolia</i>
</b> ➾ Both nomadic people with an integral horse culture and a prominent Buddha (<i>Bodhidharma in TPW, both focused on the refinement of the individual</i>) following, ruled over by the Qing dynasty/Nikara Empire.<br><br>❀ <b>
  <i>Bolonia &amp; Hesperia are America &amp; Europe</i>
</b> ➾ Strawberry blond pale skinned busybodies constantly “helping.”<br><br>I should note that TPW is inspired by <b>the Second Sino-Japanese War</b>, sparked when a dispute between Japanese and Chinese troops escalated into a full-scale invasion some scholars consider to have been the start of WWII. In TPW, Kuang grimly rewrites <b>Rape of Nanjing</b> (<i>an episode of mass murder and mass rape committed by Imperial Japanese troops</i>), revisiting the pain and consequences of those atrocities, and proceeds to finish her smaller <b>World War II</b> with thousands of Japanese soldiers remaining in China and a retelling of Hiroshima.<br><br><blockquote>
  <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601991625i/30200671._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Credit: <a href="http://www.ashleydoesartstuff.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashley Hankins</a>
</blockquote>
</blockquote><br>History aside, there is dangerous magic in TPW as much as there is war, and the author is just as thorough in capturing the mystical shamanic powers.<br><br>Often associated with indigenous and tribal societies, shamanism is a system of beliefs surrounding a spirit world that a shaman can interact with through altered states of consciousness. <b>Not only does Kuang portray this fascinating practice as accurately as possible, she also includes the structural implications of colonialism and imperialism and how rare and limited these communities have become.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988119i/30200514._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Characters: <i>Development &amp; Relationships</i></u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Rin</i>
</b> is an ambitious, vicious, stubborn character I immediately fell head over heels for, cheering as her cunning grew—that is, until she became a passive moon circling <i><b>Altan</b>.</i><br><br>I understand her need to belong leading to her nonsensical obsession, but not having a front row seat to her fantasies made the whole matter underdeveloped. Neither did it help that, while I get the suffocation of his repressed rage and wanted to pet his solemn head for his pain, Altan’s farce of patriotism was intolerable—don’t paint vengeance in flowers please. Honestly, he was too <i>tired</i> to fit the legendary shoes Kuang had him walk around in.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Children ceased to be children when you put a sword in their hands. When you taught them to fight a war, then you armed them and put them on the front lines, they were not children anymore. They were soldiers.</i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601991981i/30200680._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Credit: <a href="https://www.instagram.com/nanfe1789" rel="nofollow noopener">Nan Fe</a>
</blockquote>
</blockquote><br><i><b>Jiang</b>’</i>s eccentric head stuck in the clouds was fortunately a rare reprieve next to <i><b>Nezha</b>’</i>s efficient development (<i>surprisingly, as I initially loathed his idiotic, egoistic, unworthy arse</i>). But really, I just needed my manipulative, raging Rin back in action as a walking disaster and am pleased to announce her eventual realisation satisfied me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988119i/30200514._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>But Time For Criticism: <i>Why Not Five Stars?</i></u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There are 5 things I want from my adult fantasy, be it light or dark ➾ ❶ a careful plotting, ❷ a detailed craftsmanship, ❸ an immersive storytelling, ❹ a unique world building, and ❺ a layered theme; TPW meets 4 of those criteria with exceptional talent, yet falls flat with a disappointing thump in ❸. <b>The issue is not that Kuang’s writing is easy and unnoticeable like YA, it’s that her storytelling technique is more telling than showing.</b><br><br>Putting aside the few moments of eloquence where, after incessantly knocking on the door I was allowed in to explore, immersive description is a rare thing to stumble upon in this book, with the unfolding deaths of millions summarised to a few sentences and Rin realising she’d been hearing a voice addressed as <i>forgot to mention I’ve been hearing this since before so know this exists even though I ain’t gonna describe what it’s like m’kay?</i> I mean?? Hello? Hi. Yeah. Her telling style did not allow for a thorough exploration of some facets of the book, such as Rin and Altan’s dynamic, and that’s just a pity because this could have been <i>so much more</i>.<br><br>Additionally, when writing a book you make a choice between fast or slow pace and stick with it, but Kuang refused to do this and got stuck somewhere between the extremes of the two, too scared to dwell too long and yet too focused on slow strategy to run fast. TPW spans across 3 to 4 years and Kuang’s method for handling this—writing only short selective scenes—both helps avoid dragging the tale and hurts the book by making it disjointed, underdeveloped, and incapable of building momentum. We are repeatedly told time is passing and, just as we are getting comfortable in the story, we get kicked out and thrown back in weeks later. <b>It was perhaps akin to attempting to climb a magical mountain where your handhold vanishes after a few seconds; so the only way to get to the top and finish the book is to plunge in, climbing fast and without pause, because if you pause...well if you pause you’re done for.</b><br><br>But this was a promising debut and from the talent Kuang displayed in her first work, I know the next one is going to be magnificent. I can feel it in my bones.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988119i/30200514._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>Companions: <i>Playlist &amp; Related Reviews</i></u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <i>Book series playlist:</i>
</b> <a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/2q2P421TCjRvw6TAzVFG8y" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify URL<br><br><blockquote><blockquote><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1601988948i/30200547.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote></blockquote></blockquote></a><br><b>
  <i>Books in series:</i>
</b><br>➴ The Poppy War (The Poppy War, #1) ★★★★☆<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3582777791" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dragon Republic</a> (The Poppy War, #2) ★★★★✯<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3583008347" rel="nofollow noopener">The Burning God</a> (The Poppy War, #3) ★★★★★</span>

<div id="review_3435374210" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3435374210" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3435374210?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008239848" href="/book/show/40022965-the-poppy-war">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy">faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=cross-post">cross-post</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=review-to-come">review-to-come</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3435374210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5648481355627692680">You know when you read the first few chapters of a book and you’re overcome by a feeling, <i>a knowing</i>, that this book is going to stick with you. That you don’t know what’s going to happen next, but you can tell you’re going to love it? — <b>that’s what The Poppy War made me feel.</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>The writing was exquisite. It drew me in, and <b>kept me hooked</b>. It felt like I was <b>watching a movie in my head</b>, everything was so vivid, mesmerising but also heartbreaking. From descriptions of the setting, to the history and </span>
  <span id="freeText5648481355627692680" style="display:none">You know when you read the first few chapters of a book and you’re overcome by a feeling, <i>a knowing</i>, that this book is going to stick with you. That you don’t know what’s going to happen next, but you can tell you’re going to love it? — <b>that’s what The Poppy War made me feel.</b><br /><br /><br /><br />The writing was exquisite. It drew me in, and <b>kept me hooked</b>. It felt like I was <b>watching a movie in my head</b>, everything was so vivid, mesmerising but also heartbreaking. From descriptions of the setting, to the history and world building. Wow. I’m completely in awe of the authors skill. With each chapter I became more and more obsessed with this world and this story.<br /><br />I loved the elements of magic and mythology combined with the history and war.<br /><br />There was constantly a lot of new information to process and so many characters that I had to start keeping a log of who’s who — but honestly that just added to my enjoyment.<br /><br />The first portion is set during Rin’s time at the academy is slow paced. After that things really start picking up.<br /><br />I cannot say there was one moment I was bored or uninterested, even during the slower chapters.<br /><br /><br /><br />The setting was fantastic. I’m so used to reading western centric fantasy and this just made me realize how much <b>I need Asian fantasy in my life.</b><br /><br />Something that <b>I enjoy most as a reader is learning through fiction.</b> The author <b>draws from real Chinese historic events</b> such as the Opium Wars, the Second Sino-Japanese War and The Rape of Nanking.<br /><br />I immediately found myself looking up these events, wanting to know more. It hit me so hard to find out that all these atrocities actually happened and people don’t speak about it.<br /><br />This book while an enjoyable read was also very hard to read. It portrays the <b>very real horrors of war</b> and there were times I was crying my eyes out for all the suffering Rin had witnessed. (content and trigger warnings at the end of this review)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Rin, I admire the most. She fought tooth and nail for her place at Sinegard and didn’t let the others who thought she had no right to be there bring her down. <b>She was fierce and determined</b>. And yes, when war came knocking she realised she wasn’t as prepared as she’d thought. War and circumstances changed her and she ends up making questionable decisions that I didn’t agree with, however I still wanted the best for her (I’m still worried about her and I’m so scared for her in the next books eeeek! ).<br /><br />Altan was also another character I really enjoyed reading about. There were times I hated him but at the end of the day I think Kuang did such a great job creating this character who has been used as a weapon, treated like an animal, who is driven by vengeance and hate.<br /><br />The character growth we see in the span of one book left me shook. Some characters I thought were garbage become dear to me (*cough* Nezha *cough*). Kuang makes sure we see the flaws in every character, the basics of human nature, the cruelty humans are capable of when they think others are lesser.<br /><br />The ending left me teary eyed and with a hunger for more. I’m sad that I didn’t read this book when it came out but now I’m glad because I can immediately continue on to book 2 and there’s not much time I have to wait till the final book is released 💃.<br /><br />I really hope we get to see more development of the Cike crew. I feel like there is still so much I need to know!<br /><br /><blockquote>I have become something wonderful, she thought. I have become something terrible.<br /><br />Was she now a goddess or a monster? <br />Perhaps neither. Perhaps both.</blockquote><br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNINGS:</b> <i>violence, murder, genocide, gore, rape, animal cruelty, human experimentation, torture, mutilation</i><br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/88201550-ameerah" rel="nofollow noopener">Ameerah</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30036082-warda" rel="nofollow noopener">Warda</a><br />___<br /><i>Pre-Read</i><br /><br />I'm gonna love this. Right? <br /><br />Seriously guys, after just finishing City of Brass I cant take another disappointment</span>
  <a data-text-id="5648481355627692680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
